Seven Technical Meanings of 'Sunnah' in Hanafi Fiqh
Defining the polysemy of 'sunnah' in Hanafi terminology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the seven technical meanings of 'sunnah' in Hanafi legal texts and apply contextual clues to identify the intended meaning.

Core Idea
Sunnah has seven distinct technical meanings in Hanafi terminology.

The term 'sunnah' appears frequently in Hanafi texts, but its meaning shifts depending on context. This lesson unpacks the seven technical usages from the classical commentary 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, helping you navigate the polysemy with precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Seven Meanings
List the seven meanings as enumerated in the text: (1) the entire Shariah, (2) a legal proof (one of the four dalils), (3) what is established by the Sunnah (e.g., obligatory acts like witr), (4) a general term covering nafil (supererogatory acts), (5) nafil proper (reward for doing, no punishment for leaving), (6) the path followed in religion (the Prophetic method), and (7) the path consistently followed by the Prophet or the Companions without obligation (e.g., tarawih).
Meanings 4 and 5 are closely related; meaning 4 is broader.
2
Examine Examples from the Text
Notice how each meaning is illustrated: meaning 1 appears in 'the most entitled to leadership is the most knowledgeable of sunnah'; meaning 3 in 'witr is sunnah' from Abu Hanifah; meaning 7 in the regulation of tarawih. Understand how context (qara'in) determines the intended meaning.
3
Differentiate Between Meanings 3 and 5
Meaning 3 refers to an obligation established by Sunnah evidence (like witr being wajib), while meaning 5 refers to a purely supererogatory act. The same term 'sunnah' can carry a sense of obligation in some contexts and recommendation in others.
This distinction is critical for understanding Hanafi rulings on witr and other acts.
4
Apply Contextual Clues
When encountering 'sunnah' in a text, assess the surrounding discussion: is it about proofs (usul), obligations, or recommended acts? Use the list to deduce which meaning applies.
Practice with the example of 'sunnah' in 'sunnah of prayer' vs. 'sunnah as proof.'

Source Text

فائدة (۱) • قد يطلقُ السنة (١) ويراد به المستحب (۳) وبالعكس ، ويعلم ذلك بالقرائن الحالية (۱) إن السنة في الاصطلاح الشرعي تطلق على معان ، منها : ١. الشريعة، وبهذا المعنى وقع في قولهم : الأولى بالإمامة الأعلم بالسنة. ٢. ما هو أحد الأدلة الأربعة الشرعية، وهو ما صدر عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم غير القرآن من قول أو فعل أو تقرير. ٣. ما ثبت بالسنة، وبهذا المعنى وقع فيما روي عن أبي حنيفة أن الوتر سنة، وعليه يحمل قولهم: عيدان اجتمعا أحدهما فرض، والآخر سنة : أي واجب بالسنة، والمراد بالسنة هاهنا ما هو أحد الأدلة الأربعة. ٤. ما يعم النفل وهو ما فعله خير من تركه من غير افتراض ولا وجوب. ٥. النفل وهو ما يثاب المرء على فعله ولا يعاقب على تركه. ٦. الطريقة المسلوكة في الدين، فالمراد الطريقة المتبعة في الدين، أو أن ثبوت ذلك الأمر كان عن طريق السنة النبوية. ٧. الطريقة المسلوكة في الدين من غير وجوب ولا افتراض ونعني بالطريقة المسلوكة ما واظب عليه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولم يتركه إلا نادرا ، أو واظب عليه الصحابة ولا كصلاة التراويح. ينظر : کشاف مصطلحات الفنون (۱): ۹۷۹ - (۹۸۳) ، وسبيل الوصول» (ص۷۹). (۲) ويقابل المستحب كراهة التنزيه ، ففي البحر» (١) : ٣٣٤) : (هو مكروه كراهة تنزيه ؛ لأنها في مقابلة المستحب». وفي منحة الخالق (۲) : (۳۵) : في ترك المستحب والمندوب كراهة إلا أنه ينبغي أن تكون دون كراهة ترك السنة غير المؤكدة كما قدمه المؤلف من أن الإثم في ترك السنة المؤكدة دونه في ترك الواجب وأنه مقول بالتشكيك ولا مانع من أن تكون الكراهة كذلك تأمل ، ثم رأيت في شرح المنية» ما نصه : فالحاصل أن المستحب في حق الكل وصل السنة بالمكتوبة من غير تأخير إلا أن المستحب في حق الإمام أشد حتى يؤدي تأخيره إلى الكراهة لحديث عائشة رضي الله عنها ، بخلاف المقتدي والمنفرد ، ونظير هذا قولهم : يستحب الأذان والإقامة لمسافر ولمن يصلي في بيته في المصر ويكره تركهما للأول دون الثاني، فعلم أن مراتب الاستحباب متفاوتة كمراتب السنة والواجب والفرض ا هـ . ومثله في شرح الباقاني». وحينئذ فيكون بعض المستحبات تركها مكروها تنزيهاً، وبعضها غير مكروه، ومنه : الأكل يوم الأضحى، فإنه لو لم يؤخره إلى ما بعد الصلاة لا يكره مع أن التأخير مستحب، والمراد نفي الكراهة أصلاً خلافاً لما قدمناه عن بعض الفضلاء لما سيأتي في باب العيد من قوله : لأن الكراهة لا بد لها من دليل خاص... وبذلك يندفع الإشكال ؛ لأن المكروه تنزيها الذي ثبتت کراهته بالدليل يكون خلاف الأولى، ولا يلزم من كون الشيء خلاف الأولى أن يكون مكروهاً تنزيهاً ما لم يوجد دليل الكراهة. والحاصل أن خلاف الأولى أعم من المكروه تنزيهاً وترك
Benefit (1): Sometimes 'sunnah' is used and what is meant is 'mustahabb', and vice versa, and that is known from contextual clues. (1) Indeed, 'sunnah' in legal terminology is used for meanings, among them: 1. The Shariah, and in this sense it occurs in their statement: 'The most entitled to leadership is the most knowledgeable of sunnah.' 2. What is one of the four legal proofs, which is what issued from the Prophet, peace be upon him, other than the Qur'an, whether speech, action, or tacit approval. 3. What is established by the sunnah, and in this sense it occurs in what was narrated from Abu Hanifah that witr is sunnah, and upon this is based their statement: 'Two Eid celebrations come together, one is fard and the other is sunnah' meaning obligatory by the sunnah, and what is meant by sunnah here is one of the four proofs. 4. What includes nafil, which is something whose doing is better than leaving it, without being fard or wajib. 5. Nafil, which is something for which a person is rewarded for doing it and not punished for leaving it. 6. The path followed in religion, so what is meant is the method followed in religion, or that the establishment of that matter was through the Prophetic sunnah. 7. The path followed in religion without obligation or duty, and by 'the path followed' we mean what the Prophet, peace be upon him, consistently did and only rarely left, or what the Companions consistently did, like tarawih prayer. See: Kashshaf Istilahat al-Funun (1: 979-983) and Sabil al-Wusul (p. 79). (2) And corresponding to mustahabb is karahah tanzihiyyah, for in al-Bahr (1: 334): 'It is makruh with a tanzihi dislike because it is in contrast to mustahabb.' And in Minhah al-Khaliq (2: 35): 'In leaving mustahabb and mandub there is dislike, except that it should be less than the dislike of leaving an non-emphasized sunnah, as the author stated that the sin in leaving an emphasized sunnah is less than the sin in leaving a wajib, and that it is said by tashkik, and there is no obstacle that the dislike be likewise, ponder. Then I saw in Sharh al-Munyah its text: 'The conclusion is that mustahabb for everyone is to join the sunnah with the obligatory prayer without delay, except that mustahabb for the imam is stronger such that his delay leads to dislike due to the hadith of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, contrary to the follower and the one praying alone. Similar to this is their statement: It is mustahabb for a traveler and for one who prays in his house in the town to give adhan and iqamah, and it is disliked to leave them for the former but not the latter. Thus it is known that the levels of istihbab are varied like the levels of sunnah, wajib, and fard. End quote. And similar in Sharh al-Baqqani. Then, accordingly, some mustahabb acts become makruh tanzihan if left, and others are not makruh. Among them: eating on the day of Adha, for if he does not delay it until after the prayer, it is not makruh, although delaying is mustahabb. What is meant is the negation of dislike at all, contrary to what we presented from some scholars due to what will come in the chapter of Eid from his statement: 'Because dislike necessarily requires a specific evidence...' And thus the objection is repelled, because the makruh tanzihan whose dislike is established by evidence is khilaf al-awla, and it does not follow from something being khilaf al-awla that it is makruh tanzihan as long as no evidence of dislike exists. And the conclusion is that khilaf al-awla is more general than makruh tanzihan, and leaving mustahabb is khilaf al-awla always, not makruh tanzihan always, but it may be makruh if evidence of dislike exists, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling clarification from the Hanafi commentary 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah.' It opens with a benefit (fa'idah) regarding the multiple technical meanings of the term 'sunnah' in Hanafi fiqh. The author lists seven distinct meanings: (1) the entire Shariah, (2) one of the four primary proofs (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas), (3) an obligation established by the Sunnah but not explicit in the Qur'an (e.g., witr), (4) a general term including nafil (supererogatory) acts where doing is better than leaving without obligation, (5) nafil proper (reward for doing, no punishment for leaving), (6) the path followed in religion (the Prophetic way), and (7) the path consistently followed by the Prophet or the Companions without obligation (like tarawih). The second part discusses the ruling on leaving mustahabb (recommended) acts. The author clarifies that while leaving mustahabb is generally 'khilaf al-awla' (contrary to the better), it is not automatically makruh tanzihan (disliked). It becomes makruh tanzihan only if there is specific evidence of dislike. The author uses examples from prayer and Eid to illustrate that the levels of istihbab (recommendation) vary. This aligns with the Hanafi principle that categories like sunnah, wajib, and mustahabb have graded levels, and the ruling on neglecting them depends on the strength of the evidence.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): Polysemous term with seven technical meanings in Hanafi law: (1) Shariah, (2) legal proof, (3) established by Sunnah, (4) general nafil, (5) nafil, (6) path, (7) consistent practice.
المستحب (al-mustahabb): An act whose doing is rewarded and whose leaving is not punished; leaving it is khilaf al-awla.
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory act; rewarded for doing, no punishment for leaving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which meaning of 'sunnah' is used when Abu Hanifah says 'witr is sunnah'?
A) The Shariah
B) A legal proof
C) What is established by the Sunnah (obligatory by Sunnah)
D) Nafil

Key Takeaway
The term 'sunnah' in Hanafi fiqh has seven distinct technical meanings; context determines the intended one.

Taharah — Purification

Ruling on Leaving Mustahabb: Khilaf al-Awla vs. Makruh Tanzihan
Clarifying the ruling on leaving mustahabb and its relationship to makruh tanzihan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between khilaf al-awla and makruh tanzihan to determine the ruling on leaving a mustahabb act.

Core Idea
Leaving mustahabb is always khilaf al-awla but only becomes makruh tanzihan if there is specific evidence of dislike.

Not every failure to perform a recommended act is considered disliked. Hanafi jurists distinguish between 'khilaf al-awla' (contrary to the better) and 'makruh tanzihan' (disliked). This lesson unpacks the nuanced relationship, showing how levels of istihbab vary and when leaving a mustahabb incurs dislike.

Guided Path
1
Define Mustahabb and its Opposite
Mustahabb (or mandub) is an act whose doing is rewarded but leaving is not punished. Its opposite is makruh tanzihan (disliked without sin). The passage states that corresponding to mustahabb is karahah tanzihiyyah.
The relationship is not one-to-one; not every mustahabb left becomes makruh.
2
Understand Khilaf al-Awla
Khilaf al-awla means 'contrary to the better.' It is a general category that includes leaving mustahabb, but does not necessarily imply dislike. It is broader than makruh tanzihan.
The passage emphasizes: 'khilaf al-awla is more general than makruh tanzihan.'
3
Identify When Leaving Mustahabb Becomes Makruh Tanzihan
Leaving mustahabb becomes makruh tanzihan only when there is specific evidence (dalil khass) indicating dislike. The example of delaying the sunnah prayer for the imam (due to hadith of Aisha) shows that dislike attaches when evidence exists.
General mustahabb acts, like eating before Eid prayer, do not become makruh if left, because no specific dislike is proven.
4
Apply the Principle to New Cases
When encountering a mustahabb act, first ascertain if there is any textual evidence that leaving it is disliked. If yes, it is makruh tanzihan; otherwise, it remains merely khilaf al-awla.
This principle prevents automatic categorization of all omitted mustahabb as disliked.
5
Recognize Gradation in Istihbab
The passage notes that levels of istihbab (recommendation) vary, just like levels of sunnah, wajib, and fard. Some mustahabb acts are stronger (e.g., for the imam) and their neglect may approach dislike, while others are weaker.
This is important for fatwa: the mufti must assess the strength of recommendation.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling clarification from the Hanafi commentary 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah.' It opens with a benefit (fa'idah) regarding the multiple technical meanings of the term 'sunnah' in Hanafi fiqh. The author lists seven distinct meanings: (1) the entire Shariah, (2) one of the four primary proofs (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas), (3) an obligation established by the Sunnah but not explicit in the Qur'an (e.g., witr), (4) a general term including nafil (supererogatory) acts where doing is better than leaving without obligation, (5) nafil proper (reward for doing, no punishment for leaving), (6) the path followed in religion (the Prophetic way), and (7) the path consistently followed by the Prophet or the Companions without obligation (like tarawih). The second part discusses the ruling on leaving mustahabb (recommended) acts. The author clarifies that while leaving mustahabb is generally 'khilaf al-awla' (contrary to the better), it is not automatically makruh tanzihan (disliked). It becomes makruh tanzihan only if there is specific evidence of dislike. The author uses examples from prayer and Eid to illustrate that the levels of istihbab (recommendation) vary. This aligns with the Hanafi principle that categories like sunnah, wajib, and mustahabb have graded levels, and the ruling on neglecting them depends on the strength of the evidence.

Key Terms
المستحب (al-mustahabb): An act whose doing is rewarded and whose leaving is not punished; leaving it is khilaf al-awla.
كراهة التنزيه (karāhah al-tanzīh): A disliked act that is not sinful but better avoided; it corresponds to leaving mustahabb when evidence of dislike exists.
خلاف الأولى (khilāf al-awla): Contrary to the better; a general category that includes leaving mustahabb and may or may not involve dislike.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition turns leaving a mustahabb act from khilaf al-awla into makruh tanzihan according to the passage?
A) The act is performed by the imam
B) There is a specific evidence (dalil khass) indicating dislike
C) The act is a sunnah mu'akkadah
D) The person leaves it intentionally

Key Takeaway
Khilaf al-awla is broader than makruh tanzihan; leaving mustahabb is always khilaf al-awla, but only becomes makruh with specific evidence of dislike.

The Two Considerations of the Masdar in Hanafi Fiqh
Critical refinement of linguistic objections in a hāshiya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between the two considerations of the masdar (essence vs. multiplicity) to resolve apparent contradictions in fiqh texts regarding pluralization.

Core Idea
The masdar is not pluralized when signifying essence; when indicating multiplicity, its plural is permissible.

This passage from ʿUmda al-Riʿāya addresses objections to using the singular 'طهارة' instead of the plural 'طهارات'. The key to understanding these objections is the Hanafi distinction between two considerations of the verbal noun (masdar): one that emphasizes its essence and another that reflects multiplicity. This linguistic nuance has direct implications for how we interpret fiqh texts and resolve apparent inconsistencies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central linguistic issue
Notice that the author of Al-Hidayah used the singular 'طهارة' where the plural 'طهارات' might be expected. Several objections are raised against this choice. Your task is to understand the linguistic rule governing the pluralization of masdars.
The core rule: 'al-masdar la yuthanna wa la yujmaʿ' – the verbal noun is not dualized or pluralized.
2
Recognize the seven objections and their structure
The passage presents seven objections (from al-ʿaraḍ al-thālith to al-ʿaraḍ al-thāmin). Each objection builds on a perceived contradiction or inconsistency in the commentator's argument. Read each objection and its rebuttal carefully.
The objections are numbered: third, fourth, fifth, sixth, seventh, eighth, plus the initial objection about 'ism al-jins'.
3
Follow the rebuttals, focusing on the two considerations
The commentator's key response is that the masdar can be considered in two ways: (1) as signifying the essence (al-māhiyya) – then it is not pluralized; (2) as observed with multiplicity (tuʿtabaru bi al-taʿaddud) – then its plural is permissible. Verify how each rebuttal uses this distinction.
The two considerations are explicitly introduced in the answer to the fifth objection.
4
Understand the logical structure (major and minor premises)
The commentator applies Aristotelian logic (first figure). The major premise is 'al-masdar la yuthanna wa la yujmaʿ' (universal statement). The minor premise is 'al-ṭahāra masdar'. The conclusion: 'al-ṭahāra la tuthannā wa la tujmaʿ'. Note the debate about pronoun gender and the 'lam' for generality.
The discussion of feminine pronouns and the 'lam al-istighrāq' refines the logical formulation.
5
Apply the distinction to resolve inconsistencies
The commentator himself uses the plural 'al-ṭaharāt' in his own speech, as does the author of Al-Hidayah. Using the two considerations, explain why this is not a contradiction: they observed multiplicity, while the author chose the original (singular) as preponderant.
The resolution: 'idhā lūḥiẓa bi al-taʿaddud jāza jamʿuhu, wa idhā quṭiʿa al-naẓar ʿanhu lā yūradu jamʿan'.

وجوابه : إنّه لو أورد بلفظ «الطهارات» أورد لفظين :
أحدهما : لفظ الجمع.
وثانيهما : لفظ الواحد في ضمنه ، فبهذا الاعتبار صح إطلاق الاكتفاء على إيرادِ
الثالث : إنّ لفظ : «اكتفى» ينبئ أن الأولى كان إيراد الجمع، فاكتفى بالمفرد،
وليس كذلك.
وجوابه : إنه لا شبهة أن كثرة الطهارات تقتضي أولوية الجمع، فكأنه قال : كان الأولى بالنظر إلى كثرة الطهاراتِ إيراد الجمع ، لكنّه اكتفى بالمفرد لكونه موافقاً للأصل. الرابع: إن قوله : «إنّ المصدر لا يثنى ولا يجمع»، يقتضي أن لا يصح جمعه، وقوله : «فلا حاجة إلى لفظ الجمع» يقتضي بأنه وإن كان جائزاً لكنه لا حاجة إليه، فبين

مرجوحا.
الخامس : إنا لا نسلّم أن المصدر لا يشى ولا يجمع، ألا ترى إلى قول الفقهاء :
«گفت سجدة واحدة عن تلاوتين وتلاوات في مجلس واحد». وجوابه : إن في المصدر اعتبارين :
يجمع.
أحدهما : أن يعتبر من حيث دلالته على الماهيّة، وبهذا الاعتبار لا يثنى ولا
وثانيهما : أن يلاحظ بالتعدد، وبهذا الاعتبار يصح جمعه، وعلى هذا يحملُ كلام من جمع المصدر.
وبهذا يندفع الإيراد السادس من أن الشارح مع تصريحه بأن المصدر لا يثنى ولا يجمع قد جمعه في قوله : «مع كثرة الطهارات»، وهل هذا إلا القرار على ما عنه الفرار. وبه يندفع الإيراد السابع أيضاً وهو أنه لا يخلو إما أن يجوز جمع المصدر أو لا يجوز، على الأول لا يصح قوله : «لا يثنى ولا يجمع»، وعلى الثاني لا يصح إيراد صاحب «الهداية»، ومن سلك مسلكه في الطهارات بلفظ الجمع.

ووجه الاندفاع أن يقال : إنّ المصدر إذا لوحظ بالتعدد يجوز جمعه، وبهذا الاعتبار أورد صاحب «الهداية» وغيره لفظ الجمع ، وإذا قطع النظر عنه لا يورد جمعاً، وهو الذي اختاره المصنف ؛ لكونه أصلاً وراجحاً.
الثامن : إنّ الغرض هاهنا إنما هو توجيه عدم إيراد الجمع، فقوله: «لا يثنى»
عبث لا طائل تحته.
وجوابه : إنّ ذكره امتنان وإفادة ؛ تتميماً للقاعدة، هكذا في أكثر النسخ ، وفي بعضها مع كثرة الطهارة، وهو بحذف المضاف ؛ أي مع كثرة أنواعها، فإنّ المفرد لا كثرة
فيه.
[١]قوله : لكونها ... الخ ؛ يرد عليه أنه لا يخلو إمّا أن يكون تعليلاً آخر لقوله : «اكتفى»، وإما أن يكون تعليلاً لقوله : لا يثنى ولا يجمع»، على الأول لا بد من الواو العاطفة، وعلى الثاني يجب تذكيرُ الضمائر الراجعة إلى المصدر، واختلف الناظرونَ لتوجيه دفعه :
. فاختار أخي جلبي في «ذخيرة العقبى أنه دليل الدليل، وتأنيث الضمائر الراجعة إلى المصدر باعتبار أنه عبارة عن الطهارة، وهو مردود بأن قوله : «المصدر لا يثنى ولا يجمع»، إشارة إلى كبرى الشكل الأول.
و تقرير الكلام هكذا : الطهارة مصدر، والمصدر لا يثنى ولا يجمع، ومن المعلوم أن الكلية شرط في كبرى الشكل الأول، وذلك يقتضي أن يراد بالمصدر في قوله : لأن المصدر مطلق المصدر، لا أن يكون المصدر عبارة عن الطهارة. إلا أن يقال: إنا لا نسلّم أنه إشارة إلى كبرى الشكل الأول لم لا يجوز أن يكون إشارة إلى صغرى والكبرى محذوفة؟ بأن يقال : المصدر لا يثنى ولا يجمع ، وكلّ ما لا يثى فيه ولا يجمع فلا حاجةً فيه إلى الجمع، فينتج أنه لا حاجة في الطهارة إلى الجمع، ولا يخفى أنه تكلف. ٢. ومنهم من وجه تأنيث الضمائر بأنّ اللام الداخلة على المصدر في قوله : «لأنَّ المصدر» للاستغراق، فيصح إرجاعُ ضمائر التأنيث إليه بهذا الاعتبار، وقد يقال
The singular. Its answer: If he had used the phrase 'the purifications', he would have used two words: one is the plural word, and the second is the singular word within it. On this basis, it is correct to apply the word 'sufficed' to its usage. Third: The word 'sufficed' indicates that the first [intent] was to use the plural, so he sufficed with the singular, but it is not so. Its answer: There is no doubt that the multiplicity of purifications necessitates the priority of the plural. So it is as if he said: It would have been better, considering the multiplicity of purifications, to use the plural, but he sufficed with the singular because it agrees with the original. Fourth: His statement 'The verbal noun is not dualized or pluralized' necessitates that its plural is not valid, and his statement 'Thus there is no need for the plural' necessitates that even if it were permissible, there is no need for it. So there is contradiction between his statements. Its answer: The origin in his speech is carried on the preponderant, and what is against the preponderant is permissible but preponderated. Fifth: We do not concede that the verbal noun is not dualized or pluralized. Do you not see the words of the jurists: 'He made one prostration for two and multiple recitations in one sitting'? Its answer: The verbal noun has two considerations: One is that it is considered from the perspective of its signification of the essence; on this consideration, it is not dualized or pluralized. The second is that it is observed with multiplicity; on this consideration, its plural is valid. And upon this is carried the speech of whoever pluralized the verbal noun. And with this the sixth objection is repelled: that the commentator, despite his affirmation that the verbal noun is not dualized or pluralized, has pluralized it in his statement 'with the multiplicity of purifications'. Is this not indulging in what he fled from? And with this the seventh objection is also repelled: that it is not free from either that pluralizing the verbal noun is permissible or not. On the first, his statement 'it is not dualized or pluralized' is not valid. On the second, the author of Al-Hidayah and those who follow his path in using the plural 'purifications' is not valid. The face of repelling it is to say: The verbal noun, when observed with multiplicity, its plural is permissible. On this consideration, the author of Al-Hidayah and others used the plural. And when it is ignored, one does not use the plural, and that is what the author chose because it is original and preponderant. Eighth: The purpose here is merely to justify not using the plural. So his statement 'it is not dualized' is futile. Its answer: His mention is a favor and benefit to complete the principle. This is in most copies. In some copies, 'with the multiplicity of purification' – with deletion of the genitive, i.e., with the multiplicity of its types, for the singular has no multiplicity. His statement 'because it is a generic noun' ... it is objected that it is either another justification for his statement 'sufficed' or a justification for his statement 'it is not dualized or pluralized'. On the first, a conjunctive waw is necessary. On the second, the masculine gender of the pronouns referring to the verbal noun is required. The viewers differ in justifying its repelling. Akhi Jilabi in 'Dhakhirat al-Uqba' chose that it is the proof of the proof, and the feminization of the pronouns referring to the verbal noun is based on its being an expression for purification. This is refuted because his statement 'the verbal noun is not dualized or pluralized' is an indication of the major premise of the first figure. The formulation of the speech is: Purification is a verbal noun, and the verbal noun is not dualized or pluralized. And it is known that universality is a condition for the major premise of the first figure. That necessitates that what is meant by 'the verbal noun' in his statement 'because the verbal noun' is the absolute verbal noun, not that the verbal noun is an expression for purification. Unless it is said: We do not concede that it is an indication of the major premise of the first figure. Why is it not permissible that it be an indication of the minor premise and the major premise is omitted? By saying: The verbal noun is not dualized or pluralized, and whatever is not dualized or pluralized has no need for the plural. So it results that there is no need in purification for the plural. It is not hidden that this is a contrivance. 2. Some of them justify the feminization of pronouns because the lam entering the verbal noun in his statement 'because the verbal noun' is for generality, so it is correct to refer feminine pronouns to it on this consideration. Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hishiya) in the commentary on Al-Wiqayah. The commentator addresses seven linguistic objections to the author's use of the singular 'طهارة' (purification) instead of the plural 'طهارات' in the context of the validity of performing ablution with water. The objections and rebuttals explore the nature of the verbal noun (masdar) in Arabic grammar and its application in fiqh terminology.

The first objection states that using the plural would encompass both the plural and singular meanings, but the commentator replies that the author's word 'اكتفى' (sufficed) implies he deliberately chose the singular despite the multiplicity of purifications, because it agrees with the original (أصل).

The second objection argues that 'اكتفى' suggests the plural was initially intended, but the reply clarifies that considering the multiplicity, the plural would be preferable, yet the author opted for the singular as it matches the fundamental rule.

The third objection highlights a contradiction in the author's statements: first saying the masdar is not pluralized, then saying there is no need for the plural. The rebuttal resolves this by stating that the author's speech is to be understood according to the preponderant (راجح) meaning; what contradicts it is permissible but preponderated.

The fourth objection denies that the masdar cannot be pluralized, citing jurists' usage like 'سجدة واحدة عن تلاوتين وتلاوات'. The reply introduces two considerations: 1) the masdar as signifying the essence (الماهية) – then it is not dualized/pluralized; 2) the masdar as indicating multiplicity – then its plural is valid. This distinction is key to repelling further objections.

The fifth objection accuses the commentator of inconsistency for using 'الطهارات' while asserting the masdar is not pluralized. The reply applies the two considerations: the commentator used the plural in the sense of multiplicity, not as a pure masdar.

The sixth objection presents a dilemma: either pluralization is permissible or not. The reply again invokes the two considerations: when observed for multiplicity, pluralization is valid; otherwise, it is not. The author chose the latter as the original and preponderant view.

The seventh objection claims that the entire discussion is futile because the purpose is simply to justify not using the plural. The reply explains that mentioning the rule is a benefit to complete the principle.

Finally, the passage discusses the commentator's phrase 'لكونها اسم جنس' (because it is a generic noun) and a grammatical debate about whether it serves as a justification for 'اكتفى' or for 'لا يثنى ولا يجمع'. Akhi Jilabi's view in 'Dhakhirat al-Uqba' is that it is the 'proof of the proof', but the commentator refutes this by showing that the pronoun feminization indicates the masdar refers to purification, whereas the major premise requires the masdar to be absolute. Some scholars propose an alternative logical structure (minor premise omitted) but this is deemed contrived. Another proposed justification uses the 'lam' for generality to permit feminine pronouns.

Throughout, the Hanafi school's attention to linguistic precision in defining fiqh terms is evident.

Key Terms
المصدر (al-masdar): The verbal noun; in this passage, it refers to the word 'طهارة' (purification) and its grammatical behavior regarding dual/plural forms.
الجمع (al-jam'): The plural form of a noun; here specifically the plural 'طهارات' (purifications) versus the singular 'طهارة'.
اسم الجنس (ism al-jins): A generic noun that denotes the essence or category; the commentator says 'طهارة' is used as a generic noun, which does not require pluralization.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the commentator use 'الطهارات' (plural) in his own speech while stating that the masdar is not pluralized?
A) He made an oversight and later corrected himself.
B) He used the plural under the consideration of multiplicity, which is permissible.
C) He was quoting the author of Al-Hidayah and not asserting his own view.
D) The word 'الطهارات' is not a masdar plural but a different noun.

Key Takeaway
The masdar's pluralization is permissible when multiplicity is intended; otherwise, the singular is original and preponderant.

Taharah — Purification
advanced
8 min
Grammatical Ruling on 'Taharah': Singular vs Plural
Critical refinement of the grammatical treatment of 'taharah'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi grammatical principle governing the singular vs plural use of 'taharah' as a masdar and evaluate the arguments for preferring the singular.

Core Idea
A masdar's singular is original; plural is a secondary license only when multiplicity of types is intended.

This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya dives into the linguistic rationale behind the common Hanafi practice of using the singular 'taharah' instead of a plural form. While some jurists like the author of al-Hidayah allowed the plural when considering multiple types, the prevailing view—and the one adopted by the matn author—is to stick with the singular as the original and preponderant usage. The discussion also examines whether dualization is possible and how generic nouns relate to masdars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core linguistic contention
The matn's author chose the singular 'taharah' over the plural. This lesson explores why, examining the grammatical nature of 'taharah' as a masdar and the conditions under which pluralization is permissible.
Focus on the distinction between the masdar's basic state (singular) and its exceptional pluralization when multiplicity is explicitly considered.
2
Analyze the arguments for the singular preference
The commentator presents the view that the masdar in general does not take dual or plural, but when multiplicity of types is intended, plural is allowed. The original and preferred choice, however, remains the singular.
Note the rebuttal that the statement 'لا يثنى' (it is not dualized) is not purposeless but completes the rule.
3
Evaluate the differing interpretations of the proof structure
There is disagreement over whether the clause 'لكونها اسم جنس' (because it is a generic noun) serves as a reason for 'اكتفى' (sufficed) or for 'لا يثنى ولا يجمع'. The passage critiques these views and offers resolutions regarding masculine/feminine pronoun agreement.
Consider how the syllogistic structure (first figure) is invoked and the condition of universality in the major premise.
4
Assess the inclusivity of 'taharah' as a universal
The claim that 'taharah' includes all its types and individuals is challenged because a masdar does not inherently indicate multiplicity. The response clarifies that the inclusivity is that of a universal for its particulars, not of a whole for its parts.
The mention of 'individuals' alongside 'types' is redundant but included for clarification, distinguishing chapters (types) from sections (individuals).

لكونها اسم جنس
ووجه الاندفاع أن يقال : إنّ المصدر إذا لوحظ بالتعدد يجوز جمعه، وبهذا الاعتبار أورد صاحب «الهداية» وغيره لفظ الجمع ، وإذا قطع النظر عنه لا يورد جمعاً، وهو الذي اختاره المصنف ؛ لكونه أصلاً وراجحاً.
الثامن : إنّ الغرض هاهنا إنما هو توجيه عدم إيراد الجمع، فقوله: «لا يثنى» عبث لا طائل تحته.
وجوابه : إنّ ذكره امتنان وإفادة ؛ تتميماً للقاعدة، هكذا في أكثر النسخ ، وفي بعضها مع كثرة الطهارة، وهو بحذف المضاف ؛ أي مع كثرة أنواعها، فإنّ المفرد لا كثرة فيه.
[1]قوله : لكونها ... الخ ؛ يرد عليه أنه لا يخلو إمّا أن يكون تعليلاً آخر لقوله : «اكتفى»، وإما أن يكون تعليلاً لقوله : لا يثنى ولا يجمع»، على الأول لا بد من الواو العاطفة، وعلى الثاني يجب تذكيرُ الضمائر الراجعة إلى المصدر، واختلف الناظرونَ لتوجيه دفعه :
. فاختار أخي جلبي في «ذخيرة العقبى أنه دليل الدليل، وتأنيث الضمائر الراجعة إلى المصدر باعتبار أنه عبارة عن الطهارة، وهو مردود بأن قوله : «المصدر لا يثنى ولا يجمع»، إشارة إلى كبرى الشكل الأول.
و تقرير الكلام هكذا : الطهارة مصدر، والمصدر لا يثنى ولا يجمع، ومن المعلوم أن الكلية شرط في كبرى الشكل الأول، وذلك يقتضي أن يراد بالمصدر في قوله : لأن المصدر مطلق المصدر، لا أن يكون المصدر عبارة عن الطهارة. إلا أن يقال: إنا لا نسلّم أنه إشارة إلى كبرى الشكل الأول لم لا يجوز أن يكون إشارة إلى صغرى والكبرى محذوفة؟ بأن يقال : المصدر لا يثنى ولا يجمع ، وكلّ ما لا يثى فيه ولا يجمع فلا حاجةً فيه إلى الجمع، فينتج أنه لا حاجة في الطهارة إلى الجمع، ولا يخفى أنه تكلف. ٢. ومنهم من وجه تأنيث الضمائر بأنّ اللام الداخلة على المصدر في قوله : «لأنَّ المصدر» للاستغراق، فيصح إرجاعُ ضمائر التأنيث إليه بهذا الاعتبار، وقد يقال
يشمل جميع أنواعها، وأفرادها (٢)
في توجيهه أيضاً بأنّ قوله : «المصدر لا يثنى ولا يجمع»، نفي عام، فالمعنى شيء
من المصادر لا يثنى ولا يجمع، فبهذا الاعتبار أنت الضمائر.
. ومنهم من اختار أن قوله : لأن المصدر» دليل آخر لقوله: «اكتفى»، وإنما لم يورد الواو إيذاناً بأنه دليل مستقل، ولا يخفى ما فيه من التكلف.
. ومنهم من قال : إنه دليل ؛ لقوله : «لا يجمع»، ولم يتعرض لدليل قوله : «لا يثنى» ؛ لكونه خارجاً عما هو المقصود.
[1]قوله : يشمل جميع أنواعها وأفرادها ؛ يرد عليه أن اسم الجنس موضوع عند بعضهم لنفس الماهية ، وعند بعضهم للفرد المنتشر، وأياً ما كان فلا دلالة لـه علـى التعدد، وقد صرّح ابن أبي الحديد) في «الفلك الدائر على المثل السائر» وغيره : بأنّ المصدر إنما يدل على الماهية لا على أشخاصها، وصرّح الشارح أيضاً في «التوضيح»(۲) بأن المصدر لا يدلّ على العدد، فكيف يصح قوله هاهنا بالشمول.
والجواب عنه : بأن المراد بالشمول شمول الكلي الجزيئاته، كشمول الإنسان
لأفراده، لا شمول الكلّ لأجزائه، ولا شمول اللفظ لحقائقه.
(۲) قوله : وأفرادها ؛ يرد عليه أنه لا حاجة إلى ذكره ؛ لأنه لما ثبت شموله لانواع فبالضرورة يشمل الأفراد أيضاً، ضرورة أنّ الأفراد مندرجة تحت الأنواع. وجوابه: إنّه ذكره توضيحاً، وإشارة إلى أنَّ الكتاب تحته شيئان الباب المشتمل
على الأنواع، والفصل المشتمل على الأفراد.
فإن قلت : الأنواع أيضا أفراد للجنس، معنى أفراد أفرادها.
قلت : المراد بالأفراد هاهنا ما يندرج تحت النوع، بقرينة عطفه على الأنواع.
(۱) وهو عبد الحميد بن هبة الله المدائني المعتزلي الشيعي، عز الدين المعروف بابن أبي الحديد، الكاتب المحسن الشاعر المجيد، من مؤلفاته: «الفلك الدائر على المثل السائر»، و«ديوان شعر»، و «شرح المفصل»، و «شرح نهج البلاغة»، (٥٨٦ - ٦٥٥هـ). ينظر: «الكشف» (۲) : ۱۲۹۱)، و«هدية العارفين (١) : ٢٦٢).
(۲) «التوضيح (۱ : ٢٦٩).
Because it is a generic noun. And the rebuttal is that it is said: The masdar, if considered for multiplicity, its plural is permissible, and with that consideration the author of al-Hidayah and others used the plural form, and if one disregards that, they do not use the plural, and that is what the author chose because it is the original and preponderant. The eighth: The purpose here is only to justify not using the plural, so his statement 'it is not dualized' is purposeless. Its response: His mentioning it is a favor and benefit to complete the rule. Thus in most copies, and in some 'with the multiplicity of taharah', and it is with deletion of the annexed term, i.e., with the multiplicity of its types, for the singular does not have multiplicity. [1] His statement: 'Because it is...' etc.; it is objected that it is either another reason for his statement 'sufficed', or a reason for his statement 'it is not dualized or pluralized'. In the first case a coordinating waw is necessary, and in the second case the pronouns referring to the masdar must be masculine. The viewers differed in guiding its rebuttal: Akhi Chalabi in Dhakhirat al-Uqba chose that it is a proof of the proof, and the feminization of the pronouns referring to the masdar considering that it is an expression for taharah, and this is refuted by his statement 'the masdar is not dualized or pluralized', an indication to the major premise of the first figure. And the formulation of the statement is: Taharah is a masdar, and the masdar is not dualized or pluralized, and it is known that universality is a condition in the major premise of the first figure, and that requires that by 'masdar' in his statement 'because the masdar' is meant absolute masdar, not that masdar is an expression for taharah. Unless it is said: we do not concede that it is an indication to the major premise of the first figure. Why is it not permissible that it is an indication to the minor premise and the major premise is omitted? By saying: The masdar is not dualized or pluralized, and everything that is not dualized or pluralized has no need for plural, yielding that there is no need in taharah for plural. And it is clear that this is contrived. 2. And some of them justified the feminization of the pronouns by saying that the lam entering the masdar in his statement 'because the masdar' is for generality, so it is correct to refer feminine pronouns to it in this respect. And it may be said includes all its types and its individuals. [2] In its justification also that his statement 'the masdar is not dualized or pluralized' is a general negation, so the meaning is: no masdar at all is dualized or pluralized, so in this respect the pronouns are applied. And some of them chose that his statement 'because the masdar' is another reason for his statement 'sufficed', and the waw was not brought to indicate that it is an independent proof, and what is in it of contrivance is not hidden. And some of them said: It is a proof for his statement 'it is not pluralized', and did not address the proof of his statement 'it is not dualized' because it is outside of what is intended. [1] His statement: 'includes all its types and its individuals'; it is objected that the generic noun is posited by some for the essence itself, and by some for the non-specific individual, and whichever it is, it has no indication of multiplicity. And Ibn Abi al-Hadid in al-Falak al-Da'ir ala al-Mathal al-Sa'ir and others stated: The masdar only indicates the essence not its instances. And the commentator also stated in al-Tawdih that the masdar does not indicate number, so how can his statement here about inclusivity be correct? The response: That the intended inclusivity is the inclusivity of the universal of its particulars, like the inclusivity of 'human' for its individuals, not the inclusivity of the whole for its parts, nor the inclusivity of the word for its realities. (2) His statement: 'and its individuals'; it is objected that there is no need to mention it, because once its inclusivity of types is established, it necessarily includes individuals as well, since individuals are subsumed under types. Its response: He mentioned it for clarification, and as an indication that the book has two things: the chapter that contains types, and the section that contains individuals. If you say: Types are also individuals of the genus, meaning individuals of its individuals. I say: What is intended by 'individuals' here is what is subsumed under the type, by the context of its conjunction with types. (1) He is 'Abd al-Hamid ibn Hibat Allah al-Mada'ini al-Mu'tazili al-Shi'i, 'Izz al-Din known as Ibn Abi al-Hadid, the excellent writer and poet, from his works: al-Falak al-Da'ir ala al-Mathal al-Sa'ir, Diwan Shi'r, Sharh al-Mufassal, Sharh Nahj al-Balaghah, (586-655 AH). See: al-Kashf (2:1291), Hadiyat al-'Arifin (1:262). (2) al-Tawdih (1:269).
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the grammatical treatment of the word 'taharah' (purification) in the opening of Kitab al-Taharah. The commentator (the author of 'Umda) is analyzing whether the matn's use of 'taharah' (singular) or its plural is appropriate. The text discusses several points: (1) The word 'taharah' is a masdar (verbal noun). Masdars by default do not take dual or plural forms because they denote an abstract concept. However, when a masdar refers to multiple instances or types, it may be pluralized. The author of al-Hidayah chose the singular because it is the original and preponderant usage. (2) The statement 'لا يثنى' (it is not dualized) is not superfluous but serves to complete the rule and is a favor (imtinan) from the author. (3) There is disagreement on the role of the clause 'لكونها اسم جنس' (because it is a generic noun): is it a reason for 'اكتفى' (sufficed) or for 'لا يثنى ولا يجمع' (it is not dualized or pluralized)? The pronouns referring to the masdar are feminized because the masdar 'taharah' is treated as feminine, but some argue that the masdar should be taken in its absolute sense, not specifically as 'taharah'. (4) The claim that 'يشمل جميع أنواعها وأفرادها' (it includes all its types and individuals) is challenged because a masdar does not indicate multiplicity. The response distinguishes between inclusivity of the universal for its particulars (like 'human' for individuals) versus inclusivity of a whole for its parts. (5) The mention of 'وأفرادها' (and its individuals) is redundant since individuals are included in types, but it is added for clarification. The passage thus showcases the meticulous linguistic reasoning in Hanafi fiqh commentary.

Key Terms
مصدر (masdar): A verbal noun that denotes an action or state without reference to time, typically not dualized or pluralized in its basic form.
اسم جنس (ism jins): A generic noun that indicates an essence or a non-specific individual, often used in fiqh texts to refer to categories like 'taharah'.
كالكلّى (kully): A universal concept that applies to all its particulars, e.g., 'human' applies to Zayd, 'Amr, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the author of the matn choose the singular 'taharah' over the plural?
A) Because the plural form is grammatically incorrect for masdars.
B) Because the singular is the original and preponderant usage for a masdar, and plural is only a secondary license when multiplicity is intended.
C) Because the author of al-Hidayah always used the singular, so the matn followed suit.
D) Because the word 'taharah' is a generic noun that inherently resists pluralization.

Key Takeaway
The singular 'taharah' is the original and preferred form in Hanafi fiqh texts; pluralization is a secondary license valid only when the author intends to highlight multiple distinct types.

Linguistic Proof for the Generality of Wudu
Linguistic analysis of the word 'wudu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi commentator uses the linguistic nature of the masdar to prove that the word 'wudu' encompasses all types and individuals, and respond to objections against this inclusivity.

Core Idea
A masdar indicates the essence of an act; therefore 'wudu' covers all its forms and instances without needing a plural.

In this passage, the commentator defends the statement that the word 'wudu' includes all types (like wudu for prayer and for touching the Quran) and individuals (each specific instance). He uses the grammatical property of the masdar (verbal noun) — that it is not dualized or pluralized — to argue that it denotes a universal applying to every instance. The discussion addresses objections from linguists who claim the masdar indicates only the essence, not multiplicity. The answer clarifies that the intended inclusivity is that of a universal over its particulars, not a literal multiplicity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
The commentator asserts that 'wudu' includes all its types and individuals. This is the foundation for applying the Quranic command broadly.
2
Understand the linguistic proof
The proof is that 'wudu' is a masdar (verbal noun), and masdars are not dualized or pluralized. This indicates a single essential reality that applies universally.
This relies on the Hanafi usul principle that the masdar signifies the essence (haqiqah) of the act.
3
Examine the objection
Objectors (including Ibn Abi al-Hadid and the commentator's own work al-Tawdih) argue that the masdar indicates only the essence (mahiyyah), not multiple instances. They deny the inference of multiplicity.
4
Analyze the response
The commentator responds that the intended inclusiveness is that of a universal (kulli) over its particulars (juz'iyyat), like 'human' includes all humans, not the inclusiveness of a whole over its parts. The word 'wudu' covers every occurrence of the act.
5
Resolve the further objection about 'individuals'
Another objection questions the need to mention 'individuals' after 'types'. The commentator explains it is for clarity: types are covered in the chapter, individuals in the section.

Book of Purification: Wudu. It includes all its types and individuals. In its direction also that his saying: 'The source (masdar) is not dualized nor pluralized' is a general negation, so the meaning is: none of the sources is dualized nor pluralized, so by this consideration you [addressed] the pronouns. [2] His saying: 'Allah Almighty said' — i.e., in Surat al-Ma'idah, explaining the ruling of wudu, tayammum, and ghusl: 'O you who have believed' — this verse was revealed in year four or five after the hijrah during the expedition of Banu al-Mustaliq, and by it tayammum was legislated; as for wudu and ghusl, they were already legislated before that from the time of the obligation of prayer, but the command had not come explicitly in the Quran (1). And an address like this includes men and women, and excludes those not legally obligated by rational indication. 'When you rise to prayer' (2) — i.e., when you intend to stand for prayer, i.e., you turn to it and intend to perform it, meaning while you are in a state of hadath. 'Then wash your faces' — i.e., each of you should wash his face. 'And your hands' — coordinated with 'your faces'. 'Up to the elbows' — the limit is included within the limited according to the majority. 'And wipe' — i.e., the hands.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Al-Wiqayah, specifically the opening of the Book of Purification (Kitab al-Taharah) under the section on wudu. The commentator is defending the statement that the word 'wudu' (الوضوء) includes all types and individuals of purification. The discussion is linguistic: the source (masdar) 'wudu' indicates the essence of the act, and since it is not dualized or pluralized, it implies a single essence that encompasses all instances. The commentator addresses objections from those who claim that the source does not indicate multiplicity. The answer is that the inclusiveness intended is that of a universal over its particulars, not multiple entities. The commentator also explains that the mention of 'individuals' is for clarity. Then the passage transitions to the Quranic proof: the verse from Surat al-Ma'idah (5:6) is cited as the primary evidence for the obligation of wudu. The commentator notes that the verse was revealed after the hijrah, but wudu was already obligatory from the time prayer was first prescribed. The verse commands washing the face and hands, and wiping the head, and the commentary clarifies the meanings. This demonstrates that the ruling of wudu is established both by linguistic analysis and by explicit Quranic command.

Key Terms
المصدر (al-masdar): The verbal noun (infinitive) that indicates the essence of the action without reference to number or person.
الشمول (al-shumūl): Inclusiveness of a general term over all its individual instances, here referring to the word 'wudu' including all types and forms.
الفرد المنتشر (al-fard al-muntashir): A particular individual or instance, as opposed to the universal essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct understanding of 'inclusiveness' (shumul) of the word 'wudu'?
A) The word 'wudu' has multiple meanings.
B) The word 'wudu' is a masdar that indicates the essence, and this essence applies to all its particular instances like a universal over its particulars.
C) The word 'wudu' can be pluralized to wudu'at to indicate many types.
D) The word 'wudu' refers only to the obligatory wudu, not other types.

Key Takeaway
The masdar 'wudu' indicates a universal essence that applies to every individual instance, not a plural form.

Quranic Proof for the Obligation of Wudu
Quranic proof for the obligation of wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to cite and explain the Quranic verse (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6) as the primary proof for the obligation of wudu, and state the Hanafi ruling derived from the imperative command.

Core Idea
The imperative 'wash your faces' in the Quran is a clear command that obligates wudu for prayer.

After establishing the linguistic inclusivity of the word 'wudu', the commentator turns to the Quranic proof. He quotes the verse from Surah al-Ma'idah, which commands washing the face and hands and wiping the head. This verse is the foundational textual evidence for the obligation of wudu in the Hanafi school. The commentary explains that the command is addressed to all believers when they intend to pray, that tayammum was legislated through this verse, and that wudu was already practiced before but now has explicit divine sanction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verse and its context
The verse is Surah al-Ma'idah:6, revealed during the expedition of Banu al-Mustaliq in 4-5 AH. It introduced tayammum and made the obligation of wudu explicit.
2
Understand the legal implication of the imperative
The verb 'فاغسلوا' (wash) is an imperative (amr). In Hanafi usul, the default ruling of a command is obligation (wujub) unless there is a counter-indication.
This principle is called 'al-amr yufidu al-wujub'.
3
Note the conditional phrase
The command is linked to 'when you rise to prayer' (إذا قمتم إلى الصلاة). This indicates that wudu is required when one intends to pray and is in a state of hadath.
The phrase is interpreted as 'when you intend to stand for prayer'.
4
Recognize the scope of the address
The address 'O you who have believed' includes all believers, men and women, and excludes those not legally responsible (e.g., insane, children) by rational indication.
5
Appreciate the historical continuity
Wudu and ghusl were already obligatory from the time prayer was first prescribed, but this verse made the ruling explicit in the Quran.

(۱) وهو عبد الحميد بن هبة الله المدائني المعتزلي الشيعي، عز الدين المعروف بابن أبي الحديد، الكاتب المحسن الشاعر المجيد، من مؤلفاته: «الفلك الدائر على المثل السائر»، و«ديوان شعر»، و «شرح المفصل»، و «شرح نهج البلاغة»، (٥٨٦ - ٦٥٥هـ). ينظر: «الكشف» (۲) : ۱۲۹۱)، و«هدية العارفين (١) : ٢٦٢).
(۲) «التوضيح (۱ : ٢٦٩).

فلا حاجة إلى لفظ الجمع" (قال الله تعالى ": يَتأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا إِذَا قُمْتُمْ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ فَاغْسِلُوا وُجُوهَكُمْ ) الآية)

Book of Purification: Wudu. It includes all its types and individuals. In its direction also that his saying: 'The source (masdar) is not dualized nor pluralized' is a general negation, so the meaning is: none of the sources is dualized nor pluralized, so by this consideration you [addressed] the pronouns. And some of them chose that his saying 'because the source' is another proof for his saying 'sufficed', and he only did not mention the waw to indicate that it is an independent proof, and it is not hidden what is in it of artificiality. And some of them said: It is a proof for his saying 'does not pluralize', and he did not address the proof for his saying 'does not dualize' because it is outside what is intended. [1] His saying: 'includes all its types and individuals' is objected to: that the generic noun is placed by some for the essence itself, and by some for the particular individual; and whichever it is, there is no indication for multiplicity; and Ibn Abi al-Hadid declared in 'Al-Falak al-Da'ir 'ala al-Mathal al-Sa'ir' and others that the source indicates only the essence, not its individuals; and the commentator also declared in 'Al-Tawdih' that the source does not indicate number; so how can his saying here of inclusiveness be correct? And the answer to it: that what is meant by inclusiveness is the inclusiveness of the universal over its particulars, like the inclusiveness of 'human' over its individuals, not the inclusiveness of the whole over its parts, nor the inclusiveness of the word over its realities. (2) His saying: 'and their individuals' is objected to: that there is no need to mention it; because when its inclusiveness over the types is established, then necessarily it also includes the individuals, necessarily because the individuals are subsumed under the types. And its answer: that he mentioned it for clarification, and as an indication that the book has two things: the chapter containing the types, and the section containing the individuals. If you say: the types are also individuals of the genus, so what is the meaning of 'individuals of their individuals'? I say: what is meant by 'individuals' here is what falls under the type, by the context of its conjunction with 'types'. (1) He is Abd al-Hamid ibn Hibat Allah al-Mada'ini al-Mu'tazili al-Shi'i, 'Izz al-Din known as Ibn Abi al-Hadid, the excellent calligrapher, poet, and prolific author; among his works: 'Al-Falak al-Da'ir 'ala al-Mathal al-Sa'ir', 'Diwan Shi'r', 'Sharh al-Mufassal', and 'Sharh Nahj al-Balaghah' (586-655 AH). See: 'Al-Kashf' (2:1291), 'Hadiyat al-'Arifin' (1:262). (2) 'Al-Tawdih' (1:269). Then there is no need for the word 'plural'. (He said: Allah Almighty said: 'O you who have believed, when you rise to prayer, wash your faces' — the verse.) [1] His saying: 'then there is no need for the word plural' — this is like the result of what preceded, and it would be better to say: 'for the plural', or 'the plural form', or 'the word plural', because 'the word plural' may suggest that the intended meaning is this particular word composed of jim, mim, and 'ayn. [2] His saying: 'Allah Almighty said' — i.e., in Surat al-Ma'idah, explaining the ruling of wudu, tayammum, and ghusl: 'O you who have believed' — this verse was revealed in year four or five after the hijrah during the expedition of Banu al-Mustaliq, and by it tayammum was legislated; as for wudu and ghusl, they were already legislated before that from the time of the obligation of prayer, but the command had not come explicitly in the Quran (1). And an address like this includes men and women, and excludes those not legally obligated by rational indication. 'When you rise to prayer' (2) — i.e., when you intend to stand for prayer, i.e., you turn to it and intend to perform it, meaning while you are in a state of hadath. 'Then wash your faces' — i.e., each of you should wash his face. 'And your hands' — coordinated with 'your faces'. 'Up to the elbows' — the limit is included within the limited according to the majority. 'And wipe' — i.e., the hands.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Al-Wiqayah, specifically the opening of the Book of Purification (Kitab al-Taharah) under the section on wudu. The commentator is defending the statement that the word 'wudu' (الوضوء) includes all types and individuals of purification. The discussion is linguistic: the source (masdar) 'wudu' indicates the essence of the act, and since it is not dualized or pluralized, it implies a single essence that encompasses all instances. The commentator addresses objections from those who claim that the source does not indicate multiplicity. The answer is that the inclusiveness intended is that of a universal over its particulars, not multiple entities. The commentator also explains that the mention of 'individuals' is for clarity. Then the passage transitions to the Quranic proof: the verse from Surat al-Ma'idah (5:6) is cited as the primary evidence for the obligation of wudu. The commentator notes that the verse was revealed after the hijrah, but wudu was already obligatory from the time prayer was first prescribed. The verse commands washing the face and hands, and wiping the head, and the commentary clarifies the meanings. This demonstrates that the ruling of wudu is established both by linguistic analysis and by explicit Quranic command.

Key Terms
الأمر (al-amr): A command form in Arabic (imperative) that indicates a request to perform an act. In Hanafi usul, it defaults to obligation (wujub).
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry purification using clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
الغاية (al-ghayah): The limit or extent up to which an act must be performed, e.g., 'up to the elbows'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It made wudu obligatory for the first time.
B) It made tayammum obligatory and reaffirmed wudu which was already obligatory.
C) It made both wudu and tayammum optional.
D) It only addressed tayammum, not wudu.

Key Takeaway
The imperative 'wash' in Surah al-Ma'idah:6 is the primary Quranic proof that wudu is obligatory for prayer.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
How the Two Qira'at on 'Arjulakum' Establish the Obligation of Washing the Feet
Commentary on the wudu verse and the qira'at on the feet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that washing the feet is fard despite the jar qira'ah and apply the principle of al-jarr li al-jiwar to resolve the apparent conflict.

Core Idea
The nasb qira'ah indicates washing; the jar qira'ah is due to adjacency, so washing remains obligatory.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah examines the Qur'anic verse on wudu (al-Ma'idah:6), where the word 'arjulakum' (your feet) is recited in two different ways: one with nasb (accusative) and one with jar (genitive). The Hanafi school, following the majority of the Companions and the Sunnah, maintains that washing the feet is obligatory (fard). The jar reading is interpreted as a grammatical adjacency (al-jarr li al-jiwar) and does not change the ruling. This lesson unpacks the evidence and reasoning behind that position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two qira'at
Locate the sentence discussing the two readings of 'arjulakum'. Note that Nafi', Ibn 'Amir, al-Kisa'i, Ya'qub, and Hafs read with nasb; the others read with jar.
Both readings are mutawatir, but they have different grammatical implications.
2
Understand the grammatical implication of each qira'ah
The nasb reading makes 'arjulakum' a direct object of 'faghsilu' (wash), indicating that washing is required. The jar reading makes it follow 'bi-ru'usikum' (with your heads), suggesting wiping.
The surface meaning of the jar reading seems to support wiping.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle of al-jarr li al-jiwar
The Hanafi interpretation holds that the jar reading is due to syntactic adjacency, not to indicate wiping. The word 'arjulakum' is actually coordinated with 'wujuhakum' (faces), but the jar is caused by the proximity to 'bi-ru'usikum'.
This principle is well-known in Arabic grammar: a noun may take the genitive case because of an adjacent preposition, even if it is not actually governed by it.
4
Note the supporting evidence from hadith and consensus
The passage states that numerous hadith (with many chains) indicate the obligation of washing and the insufficiency of wiping. Moreover, Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah have unanimously agreed on washing.
Consensus (ijma') is a strong source; deviation is criticised as error.
5
State the final ruling
Based on the nasb reading, supported by hadith and ijma', the Hanafi school rules that washing the feet is fard in wudu. Wiping alone does not suffice.
This ruling is mufta bihi and is held by all Hanafi authorities.

'Then wash your faces'; that is, let each of you wash his face. 'And your hands'; conjunction to your faces. (1) Al-Suhayli said: The obligation of wudu was in Makkah, and its verse was revealed in Madinah. Al-Tabarani in 'al-Mu'jam al-Awsat' (4:174), al-Bazzar in his Musnad (4:167), and others narrated from Usamah ibn Zayd that his father told him: 'The Prophet, peace be upon him, at the beginning of revelation, Jibril came to him and taught him wudu....' 'And your feet to the ankles'; Nafi‘, Ibn ‘Amir, al-Kisa’i, Ya‘qub, and Hafs read with nasb on the lam, and others read with jar. As for the first reading, it outwardly indicates the obligation of washing the feet because 'your feet' is then conjoined to 'your faces', and it could possibly indicate wiping if conjoined to the position of 'your heads'. The second reading outwardly indicates wiping because it is then conjoined to 'your heads', and it could possibly indicate washing if it is also conjoined to the faces, and the jar is due to adjacency. Hence the schools differed on it, and the hadith with numerous chains have indicated the obligation of washing and the insufficiency of wiping, and this is what Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama‘ah have unanimously agreed upon, and whoever deviates from the community deviates into error. The details of this research along with the remaining discussions related to this verse are in 'al-Si‘ayah' (1). [1] His saying: 'He opened...etc.'; in choosing this word over 'started' and similar, there is an omen and good news for the legislator in it of attainment of opening. This answers a question raised against the author: that the title 'Book of Taharah' indicates that what is mentioned in it are the conditions related to taharah and its issues, so citing this verse here is out of its place, and from another angle, the book is set to mention fiqh issues, not to mention proofs, so what is the wisdom of citing this verse which is among the proofs? It is answered with several points explaining the subtleties of citing this verse: 1. Among them: that he opened with this verse indicating that the faqih should pay attention to the proof, for whoever does not have the faculty of derivation from the evidence is not called a faqih (2). (2) I say: The statement of al-Laknawi here is consistent with the definition of the usuliyyun for fiqh: it is knowledge of the practical legal rulings derived from their detailed evidence. Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening of the Book of Taharah (Purification) from the commentary 'Umdat al-Ri‘ayah on Sharh al-Wiqayah. The author begins by citing the Qur'anic verse of wudu (Surah al-Ma'idah: 6) and then provides extensive explanation. The first part discusses why the author used the word 'plural' and clarifies the meaning of the verse. The second part introduces the context and revelation of the verse, noting that tayammum was legislated during the expedition of Banu al-Mustaliq, while wudu and ghusl were already established from the time prayer was made obligatory, though not explicitly commanded in the Qur'an. The address includes all obligated persons, men and women. The commentary then explains the individual commands: washing the face, washing the hands up to the elbows, and wiping the head. The discussion then focuses on the word 'arjulakum' (your feet), which has two different recitations (qira'at): one with nasb (accusative) and one with jar (genitive). The nasb reading, recited by Nafi‘, Ibn ‘Amir, al-Kisa’i, Ya‘qub, and Hafs, outwardly indicates that washing the feet is obligatory because it is conjoined to 'faces'. The jar reading, recited by others, outwardly indicates wiping because it is conjoined to 'heads'. However, the author explains that the nasb reading is the one that is relied upon because it is supported by numerous hadith that obligate washing and prohibit wiping alone. This is the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama‘ah. The author criticizes any deviation from this consensus. Finally, the commentary includes a note justifying why the author opened the Book of Taharah with this verse: to emphasize the importance of evidence in fiqh and to signal that a true faqih is one who can derive rulings from proofs, not just memorize issues.

Key Terms
القراءة (al-qira'ah): A variant recitation of the Qur'an. Here, the two recitations (nasb and jar) of the word 'أرجلكم' are discussed, both being mutawatir but with legal implications.
الغسل (al-ghusl): Washing with water. In wudu, it refers to the obligation of pouring water over the limbs and flowing it over them.
المسح (al-mash): Wiping or passing wet hands over a limb. For the feet, wiping is not sufficient according to the Hanafi school.
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the scholars. Here, it refers to the agreement of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah on the obligation of washing the feet.
الجَرّ للجوار (al-jarr li al-jiwar): A grammatical principle where a noun takes the genitive case because of an adjacent preposition, even if it is not directly governed by it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason the Hanafi school holds that washing the feet is obligatory despite the jar reading?
A) The jar reading is a weak (shadhdh) recitation and therefore invalid.
B) The jar reading is interpreted as due to syntactic adjacency, and the obligation is established by the nasb reading, hadith, and consensus.
C) The jar reading applies only to a specific situation (e.g., when wearing shoes).
D) Both readings command washing, but the jar reading does so implicitly.

Key Takeaway
Despite the apparent conflict in qira'at, the Hanafi school holds that washing the feet is fard, supported by the nasb reading, hadith, and consensus, with the jar reading explained by syntactic adjacency.

The Qira'at Dispute on Washing vs. Wiping the Feet in Wudu
Commentary on qira'at dispute and its fiqh implication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that washing the feet is fard in wudu and evaluate the opposing view based on the qira'at of 'arjulakum'.

Core Idea
The nasb qira'at and overwhelming hadith evidence make washing the feet fard; wiping is invalid in Hanafi fiqh.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary addresses a classical dispute arising from the diverse qira'at (recitations) of Quran 5:6. The word 'arjulakum' (your feet) can be read with nasb or jarr, each suggesting a different ruling: washing or wiping. The commentator explains the Hanafi position, supported by ahadith and consensus, and refutes the opposing interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two qira'at
Notice that the word 'arjulakum' is recited with nasb (accusative) by some qurra' and with jarr (genitive) by others. Recognize which reading is associated with which ruling in its apparent meaning.
Nasb conjoins to 'faces' (washing); jarr conjoins to 'heads' (wiping).
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The commentator states that the nasb reading indicates washing, but also that both readings can be interpreted to support washing. The decisive proofs are the abundant ahadith (mutawatir in meaning) that explicitly command washing, and the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah.
The jarr reading is also explained as washing by conjoining to 'faces' with jarr for permissibility.
3
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence (thamarah) of this dispute: Hanafis wash the feet; those who accept wiping would only wipe. This affects the validity of wudu and all Acts depending on it.
The difference is not merely academic — it determines whether wudu is valid.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to the opposing dalil
The opponent's dalil (jarr reading) is acknowledged, but the Hanafi response shows it can be reinterpreted and is outweighed by stronger evidence (ahadith and ijma). This illustrates the method of tarjih among conflicting proofs.
5
Note the authority structure
The passage cites Quran and sunnah as primary proofs, and relies on ijma of Ahl al-Sunnah. The Hanafi position is from zahir al-riwayah, with no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
Authority weight: qat'i thubut for the verse, zanni dalala but supported by mutawatir hadith.

The Book of Purification: Wudu. He opened the book with this verse for blessing and prosperity [؟]; this is an apposition of a sentence to a sentence. 235: 'And your feet to the ankles' – Nafi', Ibn 'Amir, al-Kisa'i, Ya'qub, and Hafs read with nasb of the lam, and others read with jarr. As for the first reading, in its apparent meaning it indicates the obligation of washing the two feet, because 'your feet' in that case is conjoined to 'your faces', and it is possible that it indicates wiping by being conjoined to the place of 'your heads'. The second reading in its apparent meaning indicates wiping, because it is then conjoined to 'your heads', and it is possible that it indicates washing by being conjoined to the faces, with the jarr being for permissibility. Hence the schools differed on this, and abundant ahadith have indicated the obligation of washing and that wiping is not sufficient, and this is what Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah have unanimously agreed upon. Whoever deviates from the Jama'ah deviates into error. The details of this research along with the remaining investigations related to this verse are in al-Si'ayah (1). [1] His saying: 'He opened' etc.: in choosing this word over 'ibtada' and the like is an auspicious sign and good news for the one embarking on it that there will be an opening (fath). This refutes an objection that could be raised against the author: that the heading 'Kitab al-Taharah' indicates that what is mentioned in it are the conditions related to purity and its issues, so citing this verse here is out of place; and in another aspect, the book is set to mention fiqh issues, not proofs, so what is the reason for citing this verse which is from the proofs? It is answered with several points explaining the subtleties of citing this verse: 1. Among them: that he opened with this verse indicating that a faqih should pay attention to the proof, for one who does not have the faculty of istinbat from the proof is not called a faqih (2). (1) al-Si'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah (1): 26-35. (2) I say: the words of al-Laknawi here are consistent with the definition of the usuliyyun for fiqh: knowledge of the practical shar'i rulings derived from their detailed evidences. As in Nihayat al-Su'l (1): 22, al-Mustasfa (1): 49, Fawatih al-Rahamut (1): 12, and others. 236: 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah. 2. Among them: that a ruling is only acceptable if it is established from a shar'i proof; for there is no place for opinion in rulings. So he began with the verse that is the proof for what comes after, so that the ruling at its first occurrence in the learner's mind would be acceptable to him. ... And among them: what the commentator mentioned in his saying: 'for blessing', i.e., for seeking blessing. And among them: what he mentioned in his saying: 'And because...' etc. An objection is raised against the first proof: that blessing can be obtained from other verses as well, so the proof is not complete, for the claim is specifically the opening with this verse. Also, blessing is not dependent on the opening, because if he had mentioned it in the middle, blessing would also be obtained. As for the definition of the fuqaha': that it is a science that investigates the states of actions in terms of permissibility, prohibition, corruption, and validity, as in the Hashiyah of al-Khadimi on al-Durar, or memorizing branches with a minimum of three as in Radd al-Muhtar, or a collection of branches as in al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm, then the words of al-Laknawi are not consistent, because fiqh is the branches and issues, and one who knows them is called a faqih in the terminology of the fuqaha'. Ibn Nujaym said in al-Bahr (1: 7): 'In conclusion, fiqh according to the usuliyyun is knowledge of the rulings from their proofs. The faqih is only the mujtahid according to them. Calling a muqallid who memorizes issues a faqih is metaphorical, and it is a reality in the 'urf of the fuqaha', as evidenced by the fact that endowments and bequests to the fuqaha' refer to them. The minimum is three rulings, as in al-Muntaqa, and al-Tahrir mentions that the common usage is to call anyone who memorizes branches, with or without their proofs, a faqih.' He means: But the usuliyyun clearly stated that the reality is abandoned due to the indication of custom; in that case, the words of the waqif or testator referring to fuqaha' turn to what is customary in his time, because that is the customary reality of his words, so the original reality is abandoned, and it becomes a reality in the 'urf of the fuqaha'. As in Radd al-Muhtar (1: 378). They discussed the minimum amount that a person must memorize to be called a faqih, and they concluded that this is left to custom. We can affirm that our custom now does not call anyone a faqih except one who knows the place of rulings from the scattered chapters of fiqh such that it is easy for him to refer to them. As in al-Mawsu'ah al-Fiqhiyyah al-Kuwaitiyyah (1: 14), and others.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening of Kitab al-Taharah (Book of Purification) in a Hanafi fiqh text. The commentator begins by noting that the author opened with the Quranic verse of wudu (5:6) for blessing (tayammun), joining sentence to sentence. He then discusses the different qira'at (recitations) of the word 'أَرْجُلَكُمْ' (your feet). The qira'at with nasb (accusative) indicates washing the feet, as it is conjoined to 'وُجُوهَكُمْ' (your faces). The qira'at with jarr (genitive) indicates wiping, as it is conjoined to 'رُؤُوسِكُمْ' (your heads). However, the commentator explains that the abundant ahadith and the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah establish that washing the feet is obligatory (fard) and that wiping is not sufficient. This is the Hanafi position and the ra'jih (preferred) view. The commentator then addresses an objection: why cite a proof (dalil) in a book of fiqh issues? He gives several reasons: 1) to show that a faqih must pay attention to proofs; 2) rulings are only acceptable when based on shar'i evidence. He also notes that opening with this verse brings blessing. Later, he discusses the definition of 'faqih', contrasting the usuli definition (knowledge of rulings from detailed proofs) with the fuqaha' definition (knowledge of branches and issues). He concludes that in customary usage, a faqih is one who knows the place of rulings in the scattered chapters of fiqh, making it easy to refer to them. This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on both evidence and practical mastery of fiqh.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): An obligatory act established by definitive evidence (qat'i al-thubut), such as from Quran or mutawatir Sunnah.
مسح (mash): Wiping a limb, such as the head or feet in wudu, as an alternative to washing in some contexts.
قراءات (qira'at): The different authorized recitations of the Quran, each considered valid and transmitted through mutawatir chains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The abundant ahadith and consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah

D) The fact that washing is easier to perform

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules washing the feet as fard in wudu, not wiping, based on the nasb qira'at, overwhelming hadith evidence, and Sunni consensus.
